Have neither:
`Density`, `ProbabilityPlot`, `Histogram`, `Box`, `WordCloud`, `Parallel`, `Copula`, `Copula3D`, `Scatter`, `Scatter3D`.

**Prep / Aggregation Inventory**

| Function(s) | Prep / aggregation location |
|---|---|
| `Density`, `ProbabilityPlot`, `Box`, `Scatter`, `Scatter3D`, `Copula`, `Copula3D` | Coerce/copy/subset data, then render; no explicit `PreAgg` aggregation. |
| `Histogram` | Coerces/subsets, then internally bins and counts records by bucket/group. |
| `WordCloud` | Coerces data, uses `quanteda.textstats::textstat_frequency()`, then renames/selects frequency columns. |
| `Treemap` | Uses `SummaryFunction(AggMethod)` and aggregates inside `if (!PreAgg)` around lines 3327 and 3611-3624; also performs hierarchy/rate prep before plotting. |
| `Pie`, `Donut`, `Rosetype` | Shared pattern: `if (!PreAgg)`, coerce, resolve `SummaryFunction(AggMethod)`, then aggregate numeric vars by grouping vars. |
| `Line`, `Area`, `Step` | Shared pattern: coerce, optional melt for multi-`YVar`, subset columns, then `if (!PreAgg)` aggregate by `XVar` and optional `GroupVar`; sort afterward. |
| `River` | Similar to line-family prep: subset `YVar`, `XVar`, `GroupVar`, optional melt, then `if (!PreAgg)` aggregate by `XVar`/`GroupVar`. |
| `Bar`, `StackedBar` | S ... [truncated]

from typing import List, Optional, Union, Tuple, Dict

def standardize(
    data: pl.DataFrame,
    col_names: List[str],
    group_vars: Optional[List[str]] = None,
    center: bool = True,
    scale: bool = True,
    score_table: bool = False,
    mode: str = "train",  # "train", "apply", or "backtransform"
    score_table_data: Optional[pl.DataFrame] = None,
    debug: bool = False,
) -> Union[pl.DataFrame, Tuple[pl.DataFrame, pl.DataFrame]]:
    """
    Standardize numerical columns with optional grouping, and optionally provide a score table
    for later backtransformation or application on new data.
    
    In training mode (mode == "train"), the function computes, for each column in col_names,
    the mean and standard deviation (globally if group_vars is None, or per group otherwise)
    and then creates new standardized columns (named "<col>_Standardized").
    
    Optionally, if score_table is True, a score table (a DataFrame of group-wise means and sds)
    is returned along with the transformed data. This score table can then be used in scoring mode.
    
    In scoring mode:
      - If mode == "apply", the function applies the standardization transformation to new data,
        using the provided score_table_data.
      - If mode == "backtransform", the function reverses the transformation (backtransforms)
        the standardized values into their original scale using the provided score_table_data.
    
    Parameters:
      data (pl.DataFrame): Input data.
      col_names (List[str]): List of numerical column names to standardize.
      group_vars (Optional[List[str]]): Columns to group by. If None, standardization is computed globally.
      center (bool): Whether to subtract the mean (default True).
      scale (bool): Whether to divide by the standard deviation (default True).
      score_table (bool): In training mode, if True, also return a score table with group means and sds.
      mode (str): "train" to compute and apply standardization on training data,
                  "apply" to standardize new data using the provided score_table_data,
                  or "backtransform" to reverse the standardization.
      score_table_data (Optional[pl.DataFrame]): In scoring mode, the score table (with columns "<col>_mean" and "<col>_sd")
                                                 to use for transforming the new data. ... [truncated]

## 14. 2026-07-07T02:50:48.177Z - analytics_shinyapp_continuation - assistant

The contract is directionally strong, but I would not approve it for implementation yet. It has the right philosophy, but it still reads partly like “a better SHAP report” instead of the foundation for a decade-long explainability system.

**Major Strengths**
- Correct framing: “prediction-surface analysis” is much better than “SHAP plots.”
- Generator-first / report-renderer split is exactly right.
- Artifact-first design is strong and aligns with Shiny, reports, APIs, dashboards, and future agents.
- The section inventory is broad: global, local, grouped, time, drift, interactions, diagnostics, interpretation.
- The contract already recognizes reusable tables as primary and plots/text as derived outputs.

**Major Weaknesses**
- The public API is still too SHAP-branded. Long term, SHAP should be one contribution backend, not the conceptual center.
- The artifact schema is too loose. A top-level `list(tables = list(), plots = list(), artifacts = list())` is flexible, but not enforceable enough.
- Prediction decomposition is under-specified. It needs a strict baseline/reference-value contract.
- Feature semantics are missing. Raw features, engineered features, one-hot levels, binned values, and grouped categorical levels need one shared mapping.
- Uncertainty is mostly absent. Importance, interactions, drift, and local explanations need stability/confidence diagnostics.
- There is no computation DAG/cache contract. Without it, “compute expensive quantities once” becomes an aspiration, not an enforceable design.
- The report risks becoming exhaustive rather than insight-dense. It needs progressive disclosure and a “what should I notice first?” layer.

**Missing Analytical Capabilities**
- Explanation stability across bootstrap/subsample folds.
- Reference vs current prediction-surface drift.
- Feature contribution uncertainty intervals.
- Feature grouping for one-hot / encoded / transformed variables.
- Model comparison explanations: why model A differs from model B.
- Error cohort explanations: where explanations differ for high-error rows.
- Fairness/subgroup reliability diagnostics where protected or sensitive groups are supplied.
- Calibration/threshold context for binary explanations.
- Counterfactual or “what would need to change?” summaries, clearly labeled as non-causal.
- Monotonicity and directional consistency checks.
- Interaction selection diagnostics: why a pair was ranked as important, not just that it was.

**Missing Reusable Artifacts**
- `c ... [truncated]

## 16. 2026-07-07T03:16:38.009Z - analytics_shinyapp_continuation - assistant

Yes. If SHAP disappeared tomorrow, the current contract should not collapse. The stable center is not “contributions”; it is **model explanation as reusable evidence about prediction behavior**.

The better long-term architecture is broader than Prediction Surface / Contribution Analysis.

I would call the canonical framework:

**Model Explanation Analysis**

or, slightly more product-like:

**Model Behavior Analysis**

My preference: **Model Behavior Analysis**.

It is broad enough to include attribution, effects, counterfactuals, prototypes, surrogate models, calibration, drift, stability, error behavior, and business interpretation. “Prediction Surface” is excellent for feature effect geometry, but too narrow for prototype explanations, counterfactuals, surrogate rules, and model behavior monitoring. “Contribution Analysis” is too attribution-centered.

## 1. Truly Generic Concepts

These survive without SHAP:

- artifact-first architecture
- generator-first computation
- reports as renderers
- model prediction behavior as the analytical object
- global importance
- local explanation
- feature effects
- interactions
- grouped behavior
- time behavior
- drift/stability
- prediction decomposition, if the method supports it
- quality gates
- findings
- display plans
- computation graph/cache
- feature semantics
- reference/current comparison
- progressive report design
- QA around schemas, reproducibility, edge cases, and non-recomputation

These are architecture.

## 2. SHAP-Specific Details Masquerading As Architecture

These should be demoted to backend-specific contracts:

- `contribution_matrix` as the universal core object
- `baseline + sum(contributions) = prediction` as a universal rule
- “contribution columns” as an assumed input shape
- feature-level additive decomposition as the default mental model
- local bar/waterfall expectations
- interaction interpretation through feature-pair contribution surfaces
- terms like `Shap_`, `shap_prefix`, `TreeSHAP`, `DeepSHAP` in the core contract
- assuming every method produces row-feature additive values
- treating dependence plots as explanation outputs rather than effect-estimation outputs

The core framework should support additive attribution, but not require it.

## 3. Canonical Framework Name

Recommended:

**Model Behavior Analysis**

Submodules under it:

- `FeatureAttributionAnalysis`
- `FeatureEffectAnalysis`
- `InteractionAnalysis`
- `LocalExplanationAnalysis`
- `CounterfactualAnalysis`
- `Proto ... [truncated]

We are starting an AutoNLS redesign from first principles.

Primary repo:
AutoNLS

Reference context:
The current package has separate R6 classes:
- ModelFitter
- ModelEvaluator
- ModelScorer

The new direction:
Use one main class / one main workflow.

Core philosophy:
- fewer public functions
- flat parameters
- copy/paste examples
- one obvious path
- powerful internals hidden behind a simple API
- breaking changes are acceptable pre-product
- legacy does not shape the future

Goal:
Redesign AutoNLS into a compact, modern nonlinear curve modeling engine for understanding functional relationships.

Do not:
- preserve old APIs just for compatibility
- create three separate user-facing classes
- add app-specific code
- modify AutoQuant yet
- implement SHAP integration yet
- overbuild dashboards
- use dplyr
- use DT

fit <- AutoNLS(

fit$summary()

fit$plots()
fit$predict(new_data)
fit$score(new_data)
fit$derivative(new_data)
fit$elasticity(new_data)
fit$best_model()
fit$report()

- fitting

- model comparison
- report artifacts

# **AutoNLS**
Automated Non-Linear Least Squares and Exploratory Data Analysis in R

[Download the AutoNLS Reference Manual](docs/AutoNLS-manual.pdf)

[Dockerfile can be found here](inst/shiny/Dockerfile)


---

## **Overview**

AutoNLS is an R package built for automating non-linear regression modeling, exploratory data analysis (EDA), and interactive visualization. Whether you're an analyst or a data scientist, AutoNLS streamlines your workflow with its extensive suite of tools, user-friendly interface, and Shiny-based app for intuitive data exploration and modeling.

---

## **Key Features**

- **Non-Linear Regression**:
  - Support for 35 pre-defined models, some increasing some decreasing.
  - Custom model addition with user-defined formulas.
  - Weighted and unweighted regression support.
  - MSE or Quantile Loss Function options
  - Categorical variables are accepted
  - Automated model evaluation with metrics like RÂ², AIC, and BIC.

- **Exploratory Data Analysis (EDA)**:
  - Automated correlation analysis (Pearson vs. Spearman).
  - Interactive visualizations using `echarts4r`.
  - Pairwise scatterplots with GAM (Generalized Additive Model) fits.

- **Visualization**:
  - Comparison of model shapes and fits.
  - Scatterplots with dynamic GAM smoothing lines.
  - Comprehensive interactive plots powered by `echarts4r`.

- **Scoring and Prediction**:
  - Score new datasets using fitted non-linear models.
  - Visualize predictions interactively.

- **Shiny App:**
  - Intuitive graphical interface for non-linear regression and data analysis.
  - Fully integrated with all AutoNLS features, including data preprocessing, eda, model fitting, and scoring.
  - Ideal for users who prefer interactive analysis without writing code.

---

```r

# Install AutoNLS
devtools::instal ... [truncated]

#' Fit AutoNLS vNext models with one workflow
#'
#' @param data A data.frame or data.table.
#' @param x Predictor column name.
#' @param y Target column name.
#' @param models Character vector of model names.
#' @param weights_col Optional non-negative weights column.
#' @param loss One of "mse", "mae", "huber", or "quantile".
#' @param n_starts Number of deterministic starts per model.
#' @param seed Random seed used for start generation.
#' @param theme Plot theme metadata retained on the fit object.
#' @param huber_delta Delta used when loss = "huber".
#' @param quantile_tau Quantile used when loss = "quantile".
#' @return An AutoNLSFit R6 object.
#' @export
AutoNLS <- function(
  data,
  x,
  y,
  models = c("Hill", "Logistic", "Gompertz"),
  weights_col = NULL,
  loss = "mse",
  n_starts = 25,
  seed = 20260707,
  theme = "dark",
  huber_delta = 1,
  quantile_tau = 0.5
) {
  fit <- AutoNLSFit$new(
    data = data,
    x = x,
    y = y,
    models = models,
    weights_col = weights_col,
    loss = loss,
    n_starts = n_starts,
    seed = seed,
    theme = theme,
    huber_delta = huber_delta,
    quantile_tau = quantile_tau
  )
  fit$fit()
  fit
}

#' AutoNLS vNext fitted result object
#'
#' @export
AutoNLSFit <- R6::R6Class(
  "AutoNLSFit",
  public = list(
    data = NULL,
    x = NULL,
    y = NULL,
    weights_col = NULL,
    models = NULL,
    loss = NULL,
    n_starts = NULL,
    seed = NULL,
    theme = NULL,
    huber_delta = NULL,
    quantile_tau = NULL,
    registry = NULL,
    fit_results = NULL,
    metrics_table = NULL,
    diagnostics = NULL,
    artifacts_cache = NULL,

    initialize = function(data, x, y, models, weights_col, loss, n_starts, seed, theme, huber_delta, quantile_tau) {
      DT <- data.table::as.data.table(data)
      if (!x %in% names(DT)) stop("x column not found in data.")
      if (!y %in% names(DT)) stop("y column not found in data.")
      if (!is.null(weights_col) && !weights_col %in% names(DT)) stop("weights_col not found in data.")
      if (!is.numeric(DT[[x]]) || !is.numeric(DT[[y]])) stop("x and y columns must be numeric.")

      self$data <- data.table::copy(DT)
      self$x <- x
      self$y <- y
      self$weights_col <- weights_col
      self$models <- models

#' Built-in AutoNLS vNext model registry
#'
#' @return A named list of nonlinear model specifications.
nls_model_registry <- function() {
  eps <- 1e-8
  safe_x <- function(x) pmax(as.numeric(x), eps)

  list(
    Linear = list(
      model_name = "Linear",
      family = "linear",
      description = "Straight-line baseline for monotone functional relationships.",
      formula = "y = a + b * x",
      parameter_names = c("a", "b"),
      start_params = c(a = 0, b = 1),
      lower_bounds = c(a = -Inf, b = -Inf),
      upper_bounds = c(a = Inf, b = Inf),
      domain = "x must be numeric.",
      tags = c("linear", "baseline"),
      monotonic = "depends on b",
      supports_derivative = TRUE,
      model_function = function(x, params) {
        params[["a"]] + params[["b"]] * as.numeric(x)
      },
      derivative_function = function(x, params) {
        rep(params[["b"]], length(x))
      }
    ),
    Hill = list(
      model_name = "Hill",
      family = "saturation",
      description = "Hill saturation curve for diminishing returns and dose response.",
      formula = "y = a * x^b / (c^b + x^b)",
      parameter_names = c("a", "b", "c"),
      start_params = c(a = 1, b = 1, c = 1),
      lower_bounds = c(a = -Inf, b = eps, c = eps),
      upper_bounds = c(a = Inf, b = Inf, c = Inf),
      domain = "x should be non-negative; values are guarded at a small epsilon.",
      tags = c("saturation", "sigmoid", "diminishing_returns"),
      monotonic = "increasing when a, b, and c are positive",
      supports_derivative = TRUE,
      model_function = function(x, params) {
        xx <- safe_x(x)
        params[["a"]] * xx^params[["b"]] / (params[["c"]]^params[["b"]] + xx^params[["b"]])
      },
      derivative_function = function(x, params) {
        xx <- safe_x(x)
        a <- params[["a"]]; b <- params[["b"]]; c <- params[["c"]]
        a * (b * c^b * xx^(b - 1)) / ((c^b + xx^b)^2)
      }
    ),
    Logistic = list(
      model_name = "Logistic",
      family = "sigmoid",
      description = "Logistic growth curve with asymptote, slope, and midpoint.",
      formula = "y = a / (1 + exp(-b * (x - c)))",
      parameter_names = c("a", "b", "c"),
      start_params = c(a = 1, b = 1, c = 1),
      lower_bounds = c(a = -Inf, b = -Inf, c = -Inf),
      upper_bounds = c(a = Inf, b = Inf, c = Inf),

+---
+
+## AutoNLS vNext Preview
+
+AutoNLS is being redesigned around one main workflow for understanding functional relationships. The Phase 0 vNext API keeps the old classes in place and adds a compact fit object:
+
+```r
+library(AutoNLS)
+library(data.table)
+
+DT <- data.table(
+  Spend = seq(1, 100, length.out = 100)
+)
+DT[, Sales := 12 + 220 * Spend^1.4 / (35^1.4 + Spend^1.4) + rnorm(.N, sd = 4)]
+
+fit <- AutoNLS(
+  data = DT,
+  x = "Spend",
+  y = "Sales",
+  models = c("Linear", "Hill", "Logistic", "Gompertz", "ExponentialDecay", "PowerCurve"),
+  weights_col = NULL,
+  loss = "mse",
+  n_starts = 25,
+  theme = "dark"
+)
+```
+
+Inspect the fitted models:
+
+```r
+fit$summary()
+fit$metrics()
+fit$best_model()
+```
+
+Build comparison data for plotting:
+
+```r
+comparison <- fit$compare_plot()
+head(comparison)
+```
+
+Predict and score new data:
+
+```r
+new_data <- data.table(Spend = c(10, 25, 50, 100))
+
+fit$predict(new_data)
+fit$score(new_data)
+```
+
+Extract marginal effects and elasticity:
+
+```r
+fit$derivative(new_data)
+fit$elasticity(new_data)
+```
+
+Generate report artifacts:
+
+```r
+artifacts <- fit$artifacts()
+names(artifacts)
+
+report <- fit$report()
+```
+
+List available registry models:
+
+```r
+list_nls_models()
+```
+
+Run the vNext smoke test:
+
+```r
+qa_autonls_vnext()
+```
+
+The current vNext registry proves the pattern with `Linear`, `Hill`, `Logistic`, `Gompertz`, `ExponentialDecay`, and `PowerCurve`. The remaining legacy model library can be migrated into the registry during the next phase.
+

#' Built-in AutoNLS vNext model registry
#'
#' @return A named list of nonlinear model specifications.
nls_model_registry <- function() {
  eps <- 1e-8
  safe_x <- function(x) pmax(as.numeric(x), eps)

  list(
    Linear = list(
      model_name = "Linear",
      family = "linear",
      description = "Straight-line baseline for monotone functional relationships.",
      formula = "y = a + b * x",
      parameter_names = c("a", "b"),
      start_params = c(a = 0, b = 1),
      lower_bounds = c(a = -Inf, b = -Inf),
      upper_bounds = c(a = Inf, b = Inf),
      domain = "x must be numeric.",
      tags = c("linear", "baseline"),
      monotonic = "depends on b",
      supports_derivative = TRUE,
      model_function = function(x, params) {
        params[["a"]] + params[["b"]] * as.numeric(x)
      },
      derivative_function = function(x, params) {
        rep(params[["b"]], length(x))
      }
    ),
    Hill = list(
      model_name = "Hill",
      family = "saturation",
      description = "Hill saturation curve for diminishing returns and dose response.",
      formula = "y = a * x^b / (c^b + x^b)",
      parameter_names = c("a", "b", "c"),
      start_params = c(a = 1, b = 1, c = 1),
      lower_bounds = c(a = -Inf, b = eps, c = eps),
      upper_bounds = c(a = Inf, b = Inf, c = Inf),
      domain = "x should be non-negative; values are guarded at a small epsilon.",
      tags = c("saturation", "sigmoid", "diminishing_returns"),
      monotonic = "increasing when a, b, and c are positive",
      supports_derivative = TRUE,
      model_function = function(x, params) {
        xx <- safe_x(x)
        params[["a"]] * xx^params[["b"]] / (params[["c"]]^params[["b"]] + xx^params[["b"]])
      },
      derivative_function = function(x, params) {
        xx <- safe_x(x)
        a <- params[["a"]]; b <- params[["b"]]; c <- params[["c"]]
        a * (b * c^b * xx^(b - 1)) / ((c^b + xx^b)^2)
      }
    ),
    Logistic = list(
      model_name = "Logistic",
      family = "sigmoid",
      description = "Logistic growth curve with asymptote, slope, and midpoint.",
      formula = "y = a / (1 + exp(-b * (x - c)))",
      parameter_names = c("a", "b", "c"),
      start_params = c(a = 1, b = 1, c = 1),
      lower_bounds = c(a = -Inf, b = -Inf, c = -Inf),
      upper_bounds = c(a = Inf, b = Inf, c = Inf),
      domain = "x must be numeric.",
      tags = c("sigmoid", "growth", "saturation"),
      monotonic = ... [truncated]

#' Fit AutoNLS vNext models with one workflow
#'
#' @param data A data.frame or data.table.
#' @param x Predictor column name.
#' @param y Target column name.
#' @param models Character vector of model names.
#' @param weights_col Optional non-negative weights column.
#' @param loss One of "mse", "mae", "huber", or "quantile".
#' @param n_starts Number of deterministic starts per model.
#' @param seed Random seed used for start generation.
#' @param theme Plot theme metadata retained on the fit object.
#' @param huber_delta Delta used when loss = "huber".
#' @param quantile_tau Quantile used when loss = "quantile".
#' @return An AutoNLSFit R6 object.
#' @export
AutoNLS <- function(
  data,
  x,
  y,
  models = c("Hill", "Logistic", "Gompertz"),
  weights_col = NULL,
  loss = "mse",
  n_starts = 25,
  seed = 20260707,
  theme = "dark",
  huber_delta = 1,
  quantile_tau = 0.5
) {
  fit <- AutoNLSFit$new(
    data = data,
    x = x,
    y = y,
    models = models,
    weights_col = weights_col,
    loss = loss,
    n_starts = n_starts,
    seed = seed,
    theme = theme,
    huber_delta = huber_delta,
    quantile_tau = quantile_tau
  )
  fit$fit()
  fit
}

#' AutoNLS vNext fitted result object
#'
#' @export
AutoNLSFit <- R6::R6Class(
  "AutoNLSFit",
  public = list(
    data = NULL,
    x = NULL,
    y = NULL,
    weights_col = NULL,
    models = NULL,
    loss = NULL,
    n_starts = NULL,
    seed = NULL,
    theme = NULL,
    huber_delta = NULL,
    quantile_tau = NULL,
    registry = NULL,
    fit_results = NULL,
    metrics_table = NULL,
    diagnostics = NULL,
    artifacts_cache = NULL,

    initialize = function(data, x, y, models, weights_col, loss, n_starts, seed, theme, huber_delta, quantile_tau) {
      DT <- data.table::as.data.table(data)
      if (!x %in% names(DT)) stop("x column not found in data.")
      if (!y %in% names(DT)) stop("y column not found in data.")
      if (!is.null(weights_col) && !weights_col %in% names(DT)) stop("weights_col not found in data.")
      if (!is.numeric(DT[[x]]) || !is.numeric(DT[[y]])) stop("x and y columns must be numeric.")

      self$data <- data.table::copy(DT)
      self$x <- x
      self$y <- y
      self$weights_col <- weights_col
      self$models <- models
      self$loss <- match.arg(loss, c("mse", "mae", "huber", "quantile"))
      self$n_starts <- max(1L, as.integer(n_starts))
      self$seed <- seed
      self$theme <- theme
      self$hub ... [truncated]

#' Generate AutoNLS vNext artifacts
#'
#' @param fit An AutoNLSFit object.
#' @return A named list of data.table artifacts.
#' @export
generate_autonls_artifacts <- function(fit) {
  best <- fit$best_model()
  if (is.null(best)) stop("No converged model is available for artifacts.")

  train_data <- fit$data
  prediction_grid <- data.table::data.table(
    x = seq(min(train_data[[fit$x]], na.rm = TRUE), max(train_data[[fit$x]], na.rm = TRUE), length.out = 100)
  )
  data.table::setnames(prediction_grid, "x", fit$x)

  residuals <- fit$residuals(model = best$model_name)
  residual_summary <- data.table::data.table(
    model_name = best$model_name,
    mean_residual = mean(residuals$residual),
    median_residual = stats::median(residuals$residual),
    sd_residual = stats::sd(residuals$residual),
    min_residual = min(residuals$residual),
    max_residual = max(residuals$residual)
  )

  list(
    model_metrics = fit$metrics(),
    fitted_values = fit$fitted_values(model = best$model_name),
    residual_summary = residual_summary,
    prediction_curve = fit$score(prediction_grid, model = best$model_name),
    derivative_curve = fit$derivative(prediction_grid, model = best$model_name),
    elasticity_curve = fit$elasticity(prediction_grid, model = best$model_name),
    convergence_diagnostics = data.table::copy(fit$diagnostics),
    model_registry_table = list_nls_models()
  )
}

#' QA checks for the AutoNLS vNext Phase 0 skeleton
#'
#' @return TRUE invisibly when checks pass.
#' @export
qa_autonls_vnext <- function() {
  registry <- nls_model_registry()
  stopifnot(is.list(registry), all(c("Linear", "Hill", "Logistic", "Gompertz", "ExponentialDecay", "PowerCurve") %in% names(registry)))

  models <- list_nls_models()
  stopifnot(data.table::is.data.table(models), nrow(models) >= 6)

  set.seed(42)
  DT <- data.table::data.table(
    Spend = seq(1, 100, length.out = 80)
  )
  DT[, Sales := 3 + 2.5 * Spend + stats::rnorm(.N, sd = 2)]

  fit <- AutoNLS(
    data = DT,
    x = "Spend",
    y = "Sales",
    models = c("Linear", "Hill", "Logistic"),
    loss = "mse",
    n_starts = 5,
    seed = 42
  )

  stopifnot(inherits(fit, "AutoNLSFit"))
  stopifnot(data.table::is.data.table(fit$metrics()), nrow(fit$metrics()) >= 1)
  stopifnot(!is.null(fit$best_model()))

  new_data <- data.table::data.table(Spend = c(10, 20, 30))
  pred <- fit$predict(new_data)
  deriv <- fit$derivative(new_data)
  elas <- fit$ela ... [truncated]

## 58. 2026-07-07T16:17:23.616Z - current_projectless_megathread - tool_output

Tool output:
Exit code: 0
Wall time: 0.3 seconds
Output:
Copy everything in this box into Codex.

We are implementing AutoNLS vNext Phase 2.

Primary repo:
AutoNLS

Phase 0:
- vNext architecture
- unified API
- registry
- artifacts
- docs

Phase 1:
- 34 model registry
- stable/experimental classification
- multi-start optimizer
- prediction
- derivative
- elasticity
- artifacts
- diagnostics

Phase 2 goal:

Transform AutoNLS from a generic nonlinear optimizer into an intelligent curve-fitting engine.

The philosophy is:

Don't just fit many models.

Understand what type of curve each model represents and optimize accordingly.

Do not:
- modify AutoQuant
- implement SHAP integration
- create additional public classes
- add dplyr
- add DT
- overbuild GUIs
- break the Phase 1 public API

==================================================
1. Family-aware initialization
==================================================

Replace generic multi-start logic with model-family-aware initialization.

Families include:
- Linear
- Saturation
- Sigmoid
- Growth
- Decay
- Hyperbolic
- Power
- Logarithmic
- Weibull
- Gompertz
- Michaelis-Menten
- Richards
- Experimental

Create initialization helpers such as:

initialize_linear_model()

initialize_saturation_model()

initialize_decay_model()

initialize_sigmoid_model()

...

or one dispatcher:

generate_initial_parameters(
    model_spec,
    data,
    n_starts
)

Use data characteristics to generate starts.

Examples:

Saturation:
- asymptote near max(y)
- half-saturation near median(x)
- slope from observed curvature

Decay:
- asymptote near min(y)
- decay rate estimated from first/last observations

Linear:
- initialize from lm()

Power:
- initialize from log-log regression where appropriate

Logarithmic:
- initialize from transformed regression

Sigmoid:
- estimate midpoint from derivative or quantiles

Do not use completely random starts unless no better information exists.

==================================================
2. Domain diagnostics BEFORE fitting
==================================================

Before fitting each model:

Check:

- x > 0 requirements
- y > 0 requirements
- monotonic expectation
- sufficient unique x values
- sample size
- parameter identifiability risks
- constant x
- constant y
- impossible domains

Return structured diagnostics.

Do not simply fail.

Artifacts:

domain_diagnostics

Columns:

model

status

warning

severity

#' Fit AutoNLS vNext models with one workflow
#'
#' @param data A data.frame or data.table.
#' @param x Predictor column name.
#' @param y Target column name.
#' @param models Character vector of model names, or "all".
#' @param weights_col Optional non-negative weights column.
#' @param loss One of "mse", "mae", "huber", or "quantile".
#' @param n_starts Number of deterministic starts per model.
#' @param seed Random seed used for start generation.
#' @param optimizer One of "optim" or "nlsLM". `nlsLM` is used only when available.
#' @param quantile_level Quantile used when loss = "quantile".
#' @param huber_delta Delta used when loss = "huber".
#' @param lower_bounds Optional named vector/list overriding lower bounds.
#' @param upper_bounds Optional named vector/list overriding upper bounds.
#' @param maxit Maximum optimizer iterations.
#' @param reltol Relative tolerance for `optim`.
#' @param scale_x Logical. Fit models on scaled x.
#' @param scale_y Logical. Fit models on scaled y and back-transform predictions.
#' @param model_status One of "stable", "experimental", or "all".
#' @param theme Plot theme metadata retained on the fit object.
#' @return An AutoNLSFit R6 object.
#' @export
AutoNLS <- function(
  data,
  x,
  y,
  models = c("Hill", "Logistic", "Gompertz"),
  weights_col = NULL,
  loss = c("mse", "mae", "huber", "quantile"),
  n_starts = 25,
  seed = 42,
  optimizer = c("optim", "nlsLM"),
  quantile_level = 0.5,
  huber_delta = 1,
  lower_bounds = NULL,
  upper_bounds = NULL,
  maxit = 5000,
  reltol = 1e-8,
  scale_x = TRUE,
  scale_y = TRUE,
  model_status = c("stable", "experimental", "all"),
  theme = "dark"
) {
  fit <- AutoNLSFit$new(
    data = data,
    x = x,
    y = y,
    models = models,
    weights_col = weights_col,
    loss = match.arg(loss),
    n_starts = n_starts,
    seed = seed,
    optimizer = match.arg(optimizer),
    quantile_level = quantile_level,
    huber_delta = huber_delta,
    lower_bounds = lower_bounds,
    upper_bounds = upper_bounds,
    maxit = maxit,
    reltol = reltol,
    scale_x = scale_x,
    scale_y = scale_y,
    model_status = match.arg(model_status),
    theme = theme
  )
  fit$fit()
  fit
}

    weights_col = NULL,
    models = NULL,

#' Generate AutoNLS vNext artifacts
#'
#' @param fit An AutoNLSFit object.
#' @return A named list of data.table artifacts.
#' @export
generate_autonls_artifacts <- function(fit) {
  best <- fit$best_model()
  if (is.null(best)) stop("No converged model is available for artifacts.")

  train_data <- fit$data
  prediction_grid <- data.table::data.table(
    x = seq(min(train_data[[fit$x]], na.rm = TRUE), max(train_data[[fit$x]], na.rm = TRUE), length.out = 100)
  )
  data.table::setnames(prediction_grid, "x", fit$x)

  residuals <- fit$residuals(model = "all")
  residual_summary <- residuals[, .(
    mean_residual = mean(residual, na.rm = TRUE),
    median_residual = stats::median(residual, na.rm = TRUE),
    sd_residual = stats::sd(residual, na.rm = TRUE),
    min_residual = min(residual, na.rm = TRUE),
    max_residual = max(residual, na.rm = TRUE)
  ), by = model_name]

  list(
    model_registry_table = list_nls_models(model_status = "all"),
    model_metrics = fit$metrics(),
    fitted_values = fit$fitted_values(model = "all"),
    residual_summary = residual_summary,
    convergence_diagnostics = data.table::copy(fit$diagnostics),
    prediction_curve = fit$score(prediction_grid, model = "all"),
    derivative_curve = fit$derivative(prediction_grid, model = "all"),
    elasticity_curve = fit$elasticity(prediction_grid, model = "all"),
    best_model_summary = data.table::data.table(
      model_name = best$model_name,
      family = best$spec$family,
      status = best$spec$status,
      objective = best$objective,
      best_start_id = best$best_start_id,
      n_starts_converged = best$n_starts_converged
    )
  )
}

#' Built-in AutoNLS vNext model registry
#'
#' @return A named list of nonlinear model specifications.
nls_model_registry <- function() {
  eps <- 1e-8
  safe_pos <- function(x) pmax(as.numeric(x), eps)
  safe_den <- function(x) ifelse(abs(x) < eps, ifelse(x < 0, -eps, eps), x)
  safe_exp <- function(x) exp(pmax(pmin(x, 60), -60))
  safe_log <- function(x) log(safe_pos(x))

  spec <- function(
    model_name,
    family,
    description,
    formula,
    parameter_names,
    start_params,
    model_function,
    derivative_function = NULL,
    lower_bounds = NULL,
    upper_bounds = NULL,
    domain = "x must be numeric.",
    tags = character(0),
    monotonic = "depends on fitted parameters",
    status = "stable"
  ) {
    if (is.null(lower_bounds)) lower_bounds <- stats::setNames(rep(-Inf, length(parameter_names)), parameter_names)
    if (is.null(upper_bounds)) upper_bounds <- stats::setNames(rep(Inf, length(parameter_names)), parameter_names)
    list(
      model_name = model_name,
      family = family,
      description = description,
      formula = formula,
      parameter_names = parameter_names,
      start_params = start_params[parameter_names],
      lower_bounds = lower_bounds[parameter_names],
      upper_bounds = upper_bounds[parameter_names],
      domain = domain,
      model_function = model_function,
      derivative_function = derivative_function,
      tags = tags,
      monotonic = monotonic,
      supports_derivative = is.function(derivative_function),
      status = status
    )
  }

  registry <- list(
    Linear = spec(
      "Linear", "linear", "Straight-line baseline for monotone functional relationships.",
      "y = a + b * x", c("a", "b"), c(a = 0, b = 1),
      lower_bounds = c(a = -Inf, b = -Inf), upper_bounds = c(a = Inf, b = Inf),
      tags = c("linear", "baseline"),
      monotonic = "increasing when b is positive; decreasing when b is negative",
      model_function = function(x, params) params[["a"]] + params[["b"]] * as.numeric(x),
      derivative_function = function(x, params) rep(params[["b"]], length(x))
    ),
    Hill2Model = spec(
      "Hill2Model", "saturation", "Two-parameter Hill curve scaled to a unit asymptote.",
      "y = x^b / (a^b + x^b)", c("a", "b"), c(a = 0.5, b = 1),
      lower_bounds = c(a = eps, b = eps), upper_bounds = c(a = Inf, b = Inf),
      domain = "x should be non-negative; guarded at a small epsilon.",
      tags = c("saturat ... [truncated]

Copy everything in this box into Codex.

We are implementing AutoNLS vNext Phase 3.

Primary repo:
AutoNLS

Current state:
Phase 0:
- vNext architecture
- unified API
- model registry skeleton
- docs
- artifacts
- qa_autonls_vnext()

Phase 1:
- 34 model registry
- stable/experimental model status
- deterministic multi-start optimizer
- prediction
- derivative
- elasticity
- artifacts
- diagnostics

Phase 2:
- family-aware deterministic initialization
- pre-fit domain diagnostics
- model suitability scoring
- deterministic ranking
- optional validation split
- parameter stability
- structured failure explanations
- richer plots output
- new artifacts:
  - domain_diagnostics
  - model_suitability
  - parameter_stability
  - validation_metrics
  - ranking_summary

Phase 3 goal:
Make AutoNLS vNext reliable enough to serve as an optional curve-fitting backend for AutoQuant SHAP effect curves later.

Do not:
- modify AutoQuant yet
- implement SHAP integration yet
- create additional public R6 classes
- reintroduce ModelFitter/ModelEvaluator/ModelScorer as preferred APIs
- use dplyr
- use DT
- overbuild reporting
- break Phase 1/2 public API

==================================================
1. Interval estimation and confidence ribbons
==================================================

Add optional interval estimation for fitted curves.

Flat parameters:
- interval_method = c("none", "residual_bootstrap", "parametric_simulation")
- interval_level = 0.95
- interval_n = 200
- interval_seed = 42
- interval_models = c("best", "all")
- interval_max_rows = 1000

Behavior:
- default interval_method = "none"
- if enabled, compute lower/upper intervals for prediction curves
- preserve original-scale predictions
- support best model first
- if interval computation fails, return structured diagnostics, not a hard failure
- do not make slow intervals run by default

Artifacts:
- prediction_intervals
- interval_diagnostics

#' Fit AutoNLS vNext models with one workflow
#'
#' @param data A data.frame or data.table.
#' @param x Predictor column name.
#' @param y Target column name.
#' @param models Character vector of model names, or "all".
#' @param weights_col Optional non-negative weights column.
#' @param loss One of "mse", "mae", "huber", or "quantile".
#' @param n_starts Number of deterministic starts per model.
#' @param seed Random seed used for start generation.
#' @param optimizer One of "optim" or "nlsLM". `nlsLM` is used only when available.
#' @param quantile_level Quantile used when loss = "quantile".
#' @param huber_delta Delta used when loss = "huber".
#' @param lower_bounds Optional named vector/list overriding lower bounds.
#' @param upper_bounds Optional named vector/list overriding upper bounds.
#' @param maxit Maximum optimizer iterations.
#' @param reltol Relative tolerance for `optim`.
#' @param scale_x Logical. Fit models on scaled x.
#' @param scale_y Logical. Fit models on scaled y and back-transform predictions.
#' @param model_status One of "stable", "experimental", or "all".
#' @param validation_fraction Optional holdout fraction between 0 and 0.5.
#' @param validation_seed Seed used for validation split.
#' @param theme Plot theme metadata retained on the fit object.
#' @return An AutoNLSFit R6 object.
#' @export
AutoNLS <- function(
  data,
  x,
  y,
  models = c("Hill", "Logistic", "Gompertz"),
  weights_col = NULL,
  loss = c("mse", "mae", "huber", "quantile"),
  n_starts = 25,
  seed = 42,
  optimizer = c("optim", "nlsLM"),
  quantile_level = 0.5,
  huber_delta = 1,
  lower_bounds = NULL,
  upper_bounds = NULL,
  maxit = 5000,
  reltol = 1e-8,
  scale_x = TRUE,
  scale_y = TRUE,
  model_status = c("stable", "experimental", "all"),
  validation_fraction = 0,
  validation_seed = 42,
  theme = "dark"
) {
  fit <- AutoNLSFit$new(
    data = data,
    x = x,
    y = y,
    models = models,
    weights_col = weights_col,
    loss = match.arg(loss),
    n_starts = n_starts,
    seed = seed,
    optimizer = match.arg(optimizer),
    quantile_level = quantile_level,
    huber_delta = huber_delta,
    lower_bounds = lower_bounds,
    upper_bounds = upper_bounds,
    maxit = maxit,
    reltol = reltol,
    scale_x = scale_x,
    scale_y = scale_y,
    model_status = match.arg(model_status),
    validation_fraction = validation_fraction,
    validation_seed = validation_seed, ... [truncated]

#' Generate AutoNLS vNext artifacts
#'
#' @param fit An AutoNLSFit object.
#' @return A named list of data.table artifacts.
#' @export
generate_autonls_artifacts <- function(fit) {
  best <- fit$best_model()
  if (is.null(best)) stop("No converged model is available for artifacts.")

  train_data <- fit$data
  prediction_grid <- data.table::data.table(
    x = seq(min(train_data[[fit$x]], na.rm = TRUE), max(train_data[[fit$x]], na.rm = TRUE), length.out = 100)
  )
  data.table::setnames(prediction_grid, "x", fit$x)

  residuals <- fit$residuals(model = "all")
  residual_summary <- residuals[, .(
    mean_residual = mean(residual, na.rm = TRUE),
    median_residual = stats::median(residual, na.rm = TRUE),
    sd_residual = stats::sd(residual, na.rm = TRUE),
    min_residual = min(residual, na.rm = TRUE),
    max_residual = max(residual, na.rm = TRUE)
  ), by = model_name]

  list(
    model_registry_table = list_nls_models(model_status = "all"),
    model_metrics = fit$metrics(),
    fitted_values = fit$fitted_values(model = "all"),
    residual_summary = residual_summary,
    convergence_diagnostics = data.table::copy(fit$diagnostics),
    domain_diagnostics = data.table::copy(fit$domain_diagnostics),
    model_suitability = data.table::copy(fit$model_suitability),
    parameter_stability = data.table::copy(fit$parameter_stability),
    validation_metrics = data.table::copy(fit$validation_metrics),
    ranking_summary = data.table::copy(fit$ranking_summary),
    prediction_curve = fit$score(prediction_grid, model = "all"),
    derivative_curve = fit$derivative(prediction_grid, model = "all"),
    elasticity_curve = fit$elasticity(prediction_grid, model = "all"),
    best_model_summary = data.table::data.table(
      model_name = best$model_name,
      family = best$spec$family,
      status = best$spec$status,
      objective = best$objective,
      best_start_id = best$best_start_id,
      n_starts_converged = best$n_starts_converged
    )
  )
}

Additional Phase 3 requirement — raw-scale vs transformed fitting validation

We need to empirically test whether AutoNLS can reliably fit models on raw/untransformed data, or whether internal transformations/scaling are still required.

Add controlled validation comparing:
- raw original-scale x/y fitting
- scaled x/y fitting
- log/log1p transformed starts where appropriate
- family-specific transformed initialization only

Important:
The user-facing API should remain original-scale.
If transformations are used, they should be internal implementation details.

Add QA/validation outputs:
- convergence rate by strategy
- objective/metric comparison by strategy
- selected model by strategy
- warning/failure reasons
- whether final predictions are returned on original scale

Add docs explaining:
- AutoNLS accepts original-scale data
- internal scaling/transformations may be used for optimizer stability
- outputs/predictions/derivatives/elasticities are returned on original scale
- when users may still need manual transformations

Do not force users to pre-transform data unless diagnostics prove it is necessary.

generate_autonls_artifacts <- function(fit) {

We are implementing AutoNLS vNext Phase 3.

Primary repo:
AutoNLS

Current status:
Phase 0:
- unified architecture
- registry
- artifacts
- docs

Phase 1:
- 34-model registry
- deterministic multi-start
- prediction
- derivative
- elasticity
- diagnostics

Phase 2:
- family-aware initialization
- domain diagnostics
- suitability scoring
- deterministic ranking
- validation split
- parameter stability
- richer plots
- raw-scale validation
- original-scale API preserved

Phase 3 goal:

Transform AutoNLS from a nonlinear optimizer into an explainable curve-modeling engine.

This phase is NOT about adding more models.

It is about understanding and explaining model quality.

Do not:
- modify AutoQuant
- implement SHAP integration
- add public R6 classes
- add dplyr
- add DT
- overbuild reporting
- break the current AutoNLS() API

1. Explain WHY a model won
==================================================

The current ranking_summary should become explainable.

For every candidate model generate:

model_name
family
overall_score
ranking_position

score components:
- RMSE contribution
- MAE contribution
- validation contribution
- convergence contribution
- stability contribution
- complexity penalty
- experimental penalty
- suitability bonus

Generate deterministic explanation text.

Example:

"Hill ranked #1 because it combined the best validation RMSE with strong parameter stability and expected saturation behavior."

No LLM.
No free-form generation.

2. Explain WHY models lost
==================================================

For every rejected model generate:

reason_code

Examples:

DOMAIN_FAILURE

LOW_SUITABILITY

POOR_VALIDATION

HIGH_COMPLEXITY

UNSTABLE_PARAMETERS

FAILED_CONVERGENCE

EXPERIMENTAL_PENALTY

Generate deterministic explanation text.

model_confidence

confidence_score

validation_gap

top_model_margin

Very High

High

Base confidence on:

validation

#' Generate AutoNLS vNext artifacts
#'
#' @param fit An AutoNLSFit object.
#' @return A named list of data.table artifacts.
#' @export
generate_autonls_artifacts <- function(fit) {
  best <- fit$best_model()
  if (is.null(best)) stop("No converged model is available for artifacts.")

  train_data <- fit$data
  prediction_grid <- data.table::data.table(
    x = seq(min(train_data[[fit$x]], na.rm = TRUE), max(train_data[[fit$x]], na.rm = TRUE), length.out = 100)
  )
  data.table::setnames(prediction_grid, "x", fit$x)

  residuals <- fit$residuals(model = "all")
  residual_summary <- residuals[, .(
    mean_residual = mean(residual, na.rm = TRUE),
    median_residual = stats::median(residual, na.rm = TRUE),
    sd_residual = stats::sd(residual, na.rm = TRUE),
    min_residual = min(residual, na.rm = TRUE),
    max_residual = max(residual, na.rm = TRUE)
  ), by = model_name]
  curve_values <- private_autonls_curve_values(fit, prediction_grid)
  curve_diagnostics <- private_autonls_curve_diagnostics(fit)
  selected_model <- private_autonls_selected_model(fit)

  list(
    model_registry_table = list_nls_models(model_status = "all"),
    model_metrics = fit$metrics(),
    fitted_values = fit$fitted_values(model = "all"),
    residual_summary = residual_summary,
    convergence_diagnostics = data.table::copy(fit$diagnostics),
    domain_diagnostics = data.table::copy(fit$domain_diagnostics),
    model_suitability = data.table::copy(fit$model_suitability),
    parameter_stability = data.table::copy(fit$parameter_stability),
    validation_metrics = data.table::copy(fit$validation_metrics),
    ranking_summary = data.table::copy(fit$ranking_summary),
    prediction_intervals = data.table::copy(fit$prediction_intervals),
    interval_diagnostics = data.table::copy(fit$interval_diagnostics),
    fit_warnings = data.table::copy(fit$fit_warnings),
    fit_recommendations = data.table::copy(fit$fit_recommendations),
    curve_values = curve_values,
    curve_diagnostics = curve_diagnostics,
    selected_model = selected_model,
    prediction_curve = fit$score(prediction_grid, model = "all"),
    derivative_curve = fit$derivative(prediction_grid, model = "all"),
    elasticity_curve = fit$elasticity(prediction_grid, model = "all"),
    best_model_summary = data.table::data.table(
      model_name = best$model_name,
      family = best$spec$family,
      status = best$spec$status,
      objective = best$objective, ... [truncated]

expression(aq_shap_effect_curve_empty <- function() {
    list(values = data.table::data.table(), diagnostics = data.table::data.table(), 
        summary = data.table::data.table(), warnings = character())
}, aq_shap_effect_curve_available <- function(backend, force_unavailable = FALSE) {
    backend <- match.arg(as.character(backend)[1L], c("none", 
        "autonls"))
    if (identical(backend, "none")) {
        return(list(available = FALSE, reason = "backend_none"))
    }
    if (isTRUE(force_unavailable) || !requireNamespace("AutoNLS", 
        quietly = TRUE)) {
        return(list(available = FALSE, reason = "autonls_not_installed"))
    }
    list(available = TRUE, reason = "available")
}, aq_shap_effect_curve_models <- function(effect_curve_models) {
    models <- as.character(effect_curve_models)
    models <- models[nzchar(models)]
    if (!length(models)) 
        models <- "stable"
    if (length(models) == 1L && models %in% c("stable", "experimental", 
        "all")) {
        return(list(models = "all", model_status = models))
    }
    list(models = models, model_status = "all")
}, aq_shap_effect_curve_scalar <- function(x, default = NA_character_) {
    if (is.null(x) || length(x) == 0L) 
        return(default)
    out <- x[[1L]]
    if (is.null(out) || length(out) == 0L || is.na(out)) 
        return(default)
    as.character(out)
}, aq_shap_effect_curve_numeric <- function(x, default = NA_real_) {
    if (is.null(x) || length(x) == 0L) 
        return(default)
    out <- suppressWarnings(as.numeric(x[[1L]]))
    if (is.na(out)) 
        default
    else out
}, aq_shap_effect_curve_artifacts_from_fit <- function(fit) {
    if (is.list(fit) && all(c("curve_values", "curve_diagnostics", 
        "selected_model") %in% names(fit))) {
        return(fit)
    }
    if (is.list(fit) && !is.null(fit$artifacts) && is.function(fit$artifacts)) {
        return(fit$artifacts())
    }
    if (requireNamespace("AutoNLS", quietly = TRUE) && exists("generate_autonls_artifacts", 
        envir = asNamespace("AutoNLS"), inherits = FALSE)) {
        return(get("generate_autonls_artifacts", envir = asNamespace("AutoNLS"))(fit))
    }
    stop("AutoNLS fit did not expose vNext artifacts.", call. = FALSE)

README.md:785:AutoQuant accepts original-scale feature and SHAP contribution columns. AutoNLS may use internal scaling, log/log1p starts, or family-specific transformed initialization for optimizer stability, but returned curve values, predictions, derivatives, and elasticities remain on the original scale. README.md:4505:`generate_regression_shap_analysis_artifacts()` consumes precomputed `Shap_` columns from AutoQuant modeling/scoring outputs. It does not compute SHAP values, call `predict()`, require a model object, or use a SHAP backend package.
README.md:4669:ShapArtifacts <- AutoQuant::generate_regression_shap_analysis_artifacts(
README.md:4783:The generator-first workflow is preferred: use `generate_regression_shap_analysis_artifacts()` for analytical options, then pass the result to `RegressionShapAnalysisReport(artifact_result = reg_artifacts, ...)`. The report function is a renderer. It can still call the generator as a convenience wrapper by passing `data` plus analytical arguments through `...`, but `artifact_result` mode avoids recomputing artifacts.
README.md:4855:`generate_binary_classification_shap_analysis_artifacts()` consumes precomputed `Shap_` columns from binary classification modeling/scoring outputs. It does not compute SHAP values, call `predict()`, require a model object, or use a SHAP backend package. `positive_class` and `prediction_scale` are explicit so the report can describe whether SHAP values are contributions toward the positive class on probability, logit, margin, or unknown scale.

## 242. 2026-07-07T22:05:07.798Z - current_projectless_megathread - assistant

**Validation Results**
Passed in the running AnalyticsShinyApp with `effect_curve_backend = "autonls"`.

The Artifact Library shows these ready artifacts under `Marginal Value / Effect Curves`:

- `shap_effect_curve_values`
- `shap_effect_curve_diagnostics`
- `shap_effect_curve_summary`

Run status: `success`  
Artifacts generated: `9` total, including `8` tables and `1` text artifact.

**Bugs Found/Fixed**
Fixed effect-curve model parsing in [R/page_analysis_modules.R](C:/Users/Bizon/Documents/GitHub/AnalyticsShinyApp/R/page_analysis_modules.R:681) and [R/page_analysis_modules.R](C:/Users/Bizon/Documents/GitHub/AnalyticsShinyApp/R/page_analysis_modules.R:737).

Cause: R’s default regex treated `\\s` inside `[,\s]+` as literal `s`, so `"stable"` became `"table"`, causing AutoNLS to fail with `Unknown model(s): table`.

Fix: changed splitter to `[,[:space:]]+` for both regression and binary SHAP modules.

**Remaining Gaps**
A broad default run with interactions enabled can fail on fixture data without interaction columns: `feature_a_col and feature_b_col must exist in data`. The AutoNLS effect-curve checkpoint passes when focused on effect curves.


## 243. 2026-07-07T23:55:33.602Z - current_projectless_megathread - user

Copy everything in this box into Codex.

We need to harden SHAP interaction handling so interaction diagnostics never fail an otherwise successful SHAP run.

Primary repos:
- AutoQuant
- AnalyticsShinyApp only if adapter validation needs a small compatibility update

Problem:
A broad/default SHAP run with interaction analysis enabled can fail when required interaction columns are not available.

Example error:
feature_a_col and feature_b_col must exist in data.

This should never be a fatal error.

Core philosophy:
Interaction analysis is optional.
Missing interaction inputs should produce diagnostics and skipped artifacts, not fail SHAP generation.

Do not:
- compute SHAP values
- modify AutoNLS
- modify AutoPlots
- modify CatBoost Builder
- implement multiclass
- use DT
- silently fabricate interaction columns

==================================================
1. Guard interaction generation
==================================================

Before generating interaction artifacts, validate:

- feature_a_col exists
- feature_b_col exists
- both are present in data
- sufficient rows
- sufficient unique values
- interaction computation requested
- required SHAP columns exist

If any requirement fails:

Do NOT stop().

Instead:

Return structured diagnostics.

Skip interaction artifact generation.

Continue remaining SHAP pipeline.

==================================================
2. Structured diagnostics
==================================================

Create/extend interaction diagnostics artifact.

Fields:

status

reason_code

reason

severity

feature_a

feature_b

required_columns

available_columns

recommendation

Examples:

missing_columns

insufficient_rows

insufficient_unique_values

interaction_not_requested

interaction_backend_unavailable

unsupported_problem_type

no_candidate_pairs

Recommendation examples:

"Run SHAP without interactions."

"Specify interaction pairs."

"Generate interaction SHAP values."

"Required feature columns are missing."

==================================================
3. Artifact behavior
==================================================

When skipped:

Do not emit partial interaction heatmaps.

Do emit:

interaction_diagnostics

Optionally emit empty but valid:

interaction_importance

interaction_summary

if existing report sections expect them.

Preserve artifact contract.

==================================================
4. Report behavior
==================================================

SHAP ... [truncated]

## 258. 2026-07-08T00:06:46.564Z - current_projectless_megathread - assistant

Implemented the SHAP interaction hardening.

**Root Cause**
Optional SHAP interaction generation could pass missing/malformed or unusable interaction pair inputs into strict pair/scoring helpers. That let optional diagnostics fail the full SHAP run with errors like `feature_a_col and feature_b_col must exist in data` or empty sparse-cell scoring failures.

**Files Changed**
AutoQuant:
- [R/generate_regression_shap_analysis_artifacts.R](C:/Users/Bizon/Documents/GitHub/AutoQuant/R/generate_regression_shap_analysis_artifacts.R:821)
- [R/generate_binary_classification_shap_analysis_artifacts.R](C:/Users/Bizon/Documents/GitHub/AutoQuant/R/generate_binary_classification_shap_analysis_artifacts.R:1194)

**New Guards / Diagnostics**

Covered skip cases include:
`missing_columns`, `insufficient_rows`, `insufficient_unique_values`, `interaction_not_requested`, `no_candidate_pairs`.

Skipped interactions now emit `interaction_diagnostics` and do not emit partial/broken interaction heatmaps.

EDA -> Feature Engineering -> Model Prep -> Model Readiness / Target Analysis -> CatBoost Builder -> Model Assessment -> Model Insights -> SHAP Insights -> Report / Export.

Model Readiness maps to the existing `autoquant_model_assessment` compatibility adapter, with user-facing label “Model Readiness” and Target Analysis context. Model Assessment remains post-model terminology only; because the current implemented adapter is pre-model readiness, the true post-model Model Assessment slot is preserved as planned until a real evaluator adapter is wired.

Custom hook behavior:
- Drafts pre-stage, post-stage, and standalone Code Runner requests.
- Does not auto-run.
- Preserves `workflow_stage`, `hook_timing`, `custom_code_hook = TRUE`, `source = "manual"`.
- Does not introduce a second execution system or bypass `local_trusted`.

- Workflow QA passed: stage registry, readiness mapping, custom hook integration, workflow state summary, page contract.

- No `DT` usage found.
- No direct `AutoNLS::` calls found.
- No nested `R/` directories found.

Remaining gaps:
- Aggregate analysis module smoke QA still reports unrelated existing upstream adapter issues: AutoQuant EDA `subscript out of bounds`, binary model insights plotting argument mismatch, and a CatBoost binary upstream warning preserved as a service result.
- True post-model Model Assessment is still not wired as a distinct implemented adapter. Next milestone should be either adding that adapter or renaming/aliasing the legacy `autoquant_model_assessment` readiness id to remove the terminology ambiguity.

Yes, we can. I avoided touching the main R library and used the temp patched library because it was already available from the prior checkpoint, but the cleaner durable fix is:

```r
devtools::install("C:/Users/Bizon/Documents/GitHub/AutoQuant")
```

or, equivalently:

```r
remotes::install_local("C:/Users/Bizon/Documents/GitHub/AutoQuant")
```

For this project, installing the local AutoQuant repo into the active R 4.5.2 library would remove the need to prepend:

```r
.libPaths("C:/Users/Bizon/AppData/Local/Temp/codex_autonls_autoquant_lib")
```

The important bit is that the installed AutoQuant build must include/export the object export helpers like `ObjectToPNG()`. The default installed copy is stale right now, which is why screenshot QA failed without the temp lib.
